Answer: \begin{code}
a0 = 6
a1 = -3

a3 = -3
a4 = -7

a0 -= a2 # a0 = 6, a2 = -5
a3 = a3  # a3 = -3
a4 += a3 # a4 = -7, a3 = -3
a4 -= a2 # a4 = -2, a2 = -5
a4 -= a3 # a4 = -5, a3 = -3
a4 = a3  # a3 = -3, a4 = -3
a2 -= a3 # a2 = -5, a3 = -3
a3 += a3 # a3 = -6, a3 = -3
a3 += a3 # a3 = -12, a3 = -3
a4 -= a2 # a4 = -17, a2 = -5
a4 += a4 # a4 = -34, a4 = -3
a4 += a4 # a4 = -68, a4 = -3
a4 += a3 # a4 = -71, a3 = -6
a2 += a3 # a2 = -11, a3 = -6
a4 -= a3 # a4 = -75, a3 = -6
a4 = a2  # a2 = -11, a4 = -11
a4 = a3  # a3 = -6, a4 = -6
a1 = a4  # a1 = -3, a4 = -6, a3 = -6
a3 -= a2 # a3 = -17, a2 = -11, a4 = -6
a3 -= a1 # a3 = -20, a1 = -3, a2 = -11, a4 = -6

Answer: The code is doing the following:

\begin{code}
a0 = 1 # a0 is now 1
a1 = 7 # a1 is now 7
a2 = 1 # a2 is now 1
a3 = -6 # a3 is now -6
a4 = 3 # a4 is now 3

a0 = a0 + a4 # a0 is now 4
a0 = a1 # a0 is now 7
a1 = a1 - a0 # a1 is now -7
a0 = a0 - a1 # a0 is now 14
a1 = a1 + a0 # a1 is now 7

a0 = a2 # a0 is now 1
a1 = a4 # a1 is now 3
a0 = a0 + a2 # a0 is now 2
a3 = a3 + a2 # a3 is now -4
a4 = a4 - a3 # a4 is now 7

a4 = a3 # a4 is now -4
a4 = a3 # a4 is now -4
a3 = a3 + a3 # a3 is now -8
a3 = a3 + a3 # a3 is now -16
a3 = a3 - a0 # a3 is now -18
a3 = a3 - a4 # a3 is now -18

a1 = a1 - a0 # a1 is now 6
a2 = a2 # a2 is now 1
a1 = a4 # a1 is now 3
a1 = a2 # a1 is now 1
\end{code}

`a4` is `-18`.

Answer: I'm not sure why you would ask such a question. I'm assuming the code is incorrect and you're asking us to fix it.

On line 7, you have `a2 -= a4`. At this point, `a4` is equal to `7`, so `a2` would be `-1`.

On line 8, you have `a2 -= a3`. This would set `a2` to `-13`.

On line 10, you have `a0 -= a4`. This would set `a0` to `-14`.

On line 11, you have `a1 = a0`. This would set `a1` to `-14`.

On line 12, you have `a0 = a3`. This would set `a0` to `6`.

On line 13, you have `a3 = a2`. This would set `a3` to `-13`.

On line 14, you have `a0 -= a2`. This would set `a0` to `-19`.

On line 15, you have `a2 -= a0`. This would set `a2` to `-32`.

On line 16, you have `a0 = a3`. This would set `a0` to `6`.

On line 17, you have `a2 -= a3`. This would set `a2` to `-38`.

On line 18, you have `a1 -= a2`. This would set `a1` to `-52`.

On line 19, you have `a2 += a3`. This would set `a2` to `-32`.

On line 20, you have `a4 -= a2`. This would set `a4` to `-39`.

Therefore, `a4` would be `-39` at the end of the computation.

Answer: \begin{code}

\begin{code}
a4 = a3
a4 -= a2
a4 -= a2
a4 = a4
\end{code}

Answer: This seems a little like a homework problem, but you seem to have put some effort in. I'll try to help you out.

First, you should have a look at the [python docs](https://docs.python.org/3/reference/expressions.html#evaluation-order) to find out how the expressions are evaluated.

The first thing you need to do is figure out the order of operations. This is done by first evaluating the right-hand side expressions (RHS), and then assigning the result to the variable on the left-hand side (LHS).

Now, lets take it step by step.

\begin{code}
a0=4; a1=8; a2=3; a3=-1; a4=-6
\end{code}

This is just assignment, so we'll just skip to the following line.

\begin{code}
a2 -= a4
\end{code}

This is a subtraction. So first we evaluate the RHS, which is a4. This is -6. Now we evaluate the LHS, which is a2. This is 3. Therefore we subtract -6 from 3, which is 9. So now a2 is 9.

\begin{code}
a3 -= a2
\end{code}

Same as the last step. RHS is 9, LHS is -1. -1 - 9 is -10. So a3 is -10.

\begin{code}
a4 -= a3
\end{code}

This one is tricky. When we evaluate the RHS, we need to get the value of a3, which is -10. Now we need to evaluate the LHS. This will give us the value of a4, which is -6. We subtract -10 from -6, which is 4. So a4 is now 4.

\begin{code}
a3 -= a2
\end{code}

This one is similar to the first one. RHS is 9, LHS is -10. We subtract 9 from -10, which is -19. So a3 is -19.

\begin{code}
a4 -= a3
\end{code}

RHS is -19, LHS is 4. We subtract -19 from 4, which is 23. So a4 is now 23.

\begin{code}
a4 = a2
\end{code}

We set a4 to 9.

\begin{code}
a4 = a3
\end{code}

We set a4 to -19.

\begin{code}
a4 = a2
\end{code}

We set a4 back to 9.

\begin{code}
a4 = a4
\end{code}

This is a no-op.

\begin{code}
a2 += a3
\end{code}

RHS is -19, LHS is 9. We add -19 to 9, which is -10. So a2 is -10.

\begin{code}
a3 = a3
\end{code}

Does nothing, because a3 is already -19.

\begin{code}
a2 -= a4
\end{code}

RHS is 9, LHS is -10. We subtract 9 from -10, which is -19. So a2 is -19.

\begin{code}
a4 += a2
\end{code}

RHS is -19, LHS is 9. We add -19 to 9, which is -28. So a4 is -28.

\begin{code}
a3 -= a2
\end{code}

RHS is -19, LHS is -19. We subtract -19 from -19, which is 0. So a3 is 0.

\begin{code}
a2 += a3
\end{code}

RHS is 0, LHS is -19. We add 0 to -19, which is -19. So a2 is -19.

\begin{code}
a3 -= a2
\end{code}

RHS is -19, LHS is 0. We subtract -19 from 0, which is 19. So a3 is 19.

\begin{code}
a4 += a3
\end{code}

RHS is 19, LHS is -28. We add 19 to -28, which is -9. So a4 is -9.

\begin{code}
a4 = a3
\end{code}

We set a4 to 19.

\begin{code}
a4 = a2
\end{code}

We set a4 to -19.

\begin{code}
a4 = a4
\end{code}

No-op.

\begin{code}
a4 = a3
\end{code}

We set a4 to 19.

So in the end, a4 is 19.

Comment: @LeeNeverGup Sorry, I'm asking the answer to the problem.

Answer: The assignment operator `=` in python first evaluates the right hand side (RHS) expression and then assigns the value to the variable.  It does not evaluate the expression in place.  So the value of `a4` is not changed by any of the assignments.  It is still `6`.

Comment: a4 is a list of integers.

Answer: Your code is just doing the same thing over and over, so I'm going to assume you forgot to include a loop in your question.

Here is your code with some line numbers added:

\begin{code}
1 a0=7; a1=-8; a2=7; a3=0; a4=-5
2 a0 = a2
3 a0 = a2
4 a0 -= a4
5 a1 = a1
6 a1 += a0
7 a0 = a0
8 a0 = a1
9 a0 -= a1
10 a1 += a4
11 a3 += a2
12 a4 += a2
13 a4 += a3
14 a2 = a2
15 a3 -= a4
16 a4 += a3
17 a3 = a1
18 a3 = a1
19 a3 = a2
20 a0 = a2
21 a2 -= a3
\end{code}

The first time it runs, the value of `a4` is increased by `a0`, which is 7.

\begin{code}
a4 = a4 + a0 = -5 + 7 = 2
\end{code}

The second time it runs, the value of `a4` is increased by `a0`, which is 2.

\begin{code}
a4 = a4 + a0 = 2 + 2 = 4
\end{code}

The third time it runs, the value of `a4` is increased by `a0`, which is now 4.

\begin{code}
a4 = a4 + a0 = 4 + 4 = 8
\end{code}

And so on. So at the end of the program, the value of `a4` is 8.

Answer: This is a very weird code, but I'm assuming you wanted to know the value of `a4` after all of the operations.

What the code does is that it:
\begin{itemize}
\item Takes 5 variables, `a0, a1, a2, a3, a4`
\item Assigns `a0` to `a2`
\item Subtracts `a4` from `a0`
\item Adds `a0` to `a1`
\item Assigns `a0` to `a1`
\item Subtracts `a1` from `a0`
\item Adds `a4` to `a1`
\item Adds `a2` to `a3`
\item Adds `a2` to `a4`
\item Adds `a3` to `a4`
\item Assigns `a3` to `a4`
\item Subtracts `a4` from `a3`
\item Adds `a3` to `a4`
\item Assigns `a0` to `a3`
\item Assigns `a1` to `a3`
\item Assigns `a2` to `a3`
\item Assigns `a2` to `a0`
\item Subtracts `a3` from `a2`
\end{itemize}

So the final value of `a4` is:

\begin{code}
a4 = a4 + a0 - a2 + a4 + a3 - a3 + a3
\end{code}

Where `a0` is `a2`, which is `7`,

`a2` is `7` as well,

`a3` is `0`, and

`a4` is `-5`.

So the final value of `a4` is `2`.

Answer: \begin{code}
a0=7; a1=-2; a2=6; a3=-9; a4=-1
a0 += a3  # a0 = 7+(-9) = -2
a0 += a4 # a0 = -2+(-1) = -3
a0 -= a1 # a0 = -3 + 2 = -1
a0 = a0 # a0 = -1
a4 += a3 # a4 = -1+(-9) = -10
a4 -= a3 # a4 = -10-(-9) = -1
a4 -= a2 # a4 = -1-6 = -7
a4 -= a3 # a4 = -7-(-9) = -2
a4 += a2 # a4 = -2+6 = 4
a4 = a2 # a4 = 6
a4 = a2 # a4 = 6
a4 += a2 # a4 = 6+6 = 12
a4 += a2 # a4 = 12+6 = 18
a2 = a3 # a2 = -9
a2 += a2 # a2 = -9+(-9) = -18
a2 = a1 # a2 = 2
a3 -= a0 # a3 = -9-(-1) = -8
a1 = a1 # a1 = -2
a0 += a3 # a0 = -1+(-8) = -9
a2 += a2 # a2 = 2+2 = 4
\end{code}

So at the end a4 = 18.

Answer: \begin{code}
a0=-6; a1=2; a2=-9; a3=3; a4=8
\end{code}

a1=2, a2=-9, a3=3, a4=8

\begin{code}
a1 = a2
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-9, a3=3, a4=8

\begin{code}
a2 -= a4
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-17, a3=3, a4=8

\begin{code}
a3 = a4
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-17, a3=8, a4=8

\begin{code}
a3 = a4
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-17, a3=8, a4=8

\begin{code}
a3 = a3
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-17, a3=8, a4=8

\begin{code}
a4 = a4
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-17, a3=8, a4=8

\begin{code}
a4 += a3
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-17, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a4 = a3
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-17, a3=8, a4=8

\begin{code}
a2 += a4
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-9, a3=8, a4=8

\begin{code}
a4 += a3
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=-9, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a2 = a3
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=8, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a2 = a2
\end{code}

a1=-9, a2=8, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a0 = a1
\end{code}

a0=-9, a1=-9, a2=8, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a0 += a0
\end{code}

a0=-18, a1=-9, a2=8, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a0 += a1
\end{code}

a0=-27, a1=-9, a2=8, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a0 = a4
\end{code}

a0=16, a1=-9, a2=8, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a2 -= a1
\end{code}

a0=16, a1=-9, a2=-1, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a1 = a1
\end{code}

a0=16, a1=-9, a2=-1, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a2 -= a4
\end{code}

a0=16, a1=-9, a2=-17, a3=8, a4=16

\begin{code}
a1 = a3
\end{code}

a0=16, a1=8, a2=-17, a3=8, a4=16

There are no more instructions. a4=16.

import inspect

class Solution:
    def __init__(self, a, b):
        self.a = a
        self.b = b

    def __str__(self):
        return '<result>{}</result>'.format(self.a + self.b)

def main():
    # read input
    a0 = int(input())
    a1 = int(input())
    a2 = int(input())
    a3 = int(input())
    # perform operations
    a1 += a2
    a0 += a0
    a4 = a4
    a4 += a2
    a2 += a2
    a4 += a3
    a4 += a4
    a4 = a3
    a3 = a2
    a4 += a4
    a3 -= a4
    a3 += a2
    a4 = a3
    a3 += a4
    a2 -= a1
    a2 = a4
    a1 = a1
    a1 -= a2
    a2 -= a3
    a2 -= a3
    # print result
    print(Solution(a0, a1))

if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()

Answer: \begin{code}
a0 = 4; a1 = -10; a2 = 3; a3 = -3; a4 = 8
a0 = a2 = 3
a1 -= a4 = -10 - 8 = -18
a2 -= a4 = 3 - 8 = -5
a2 -= a4 = -5 - 8 = -13
a3 = a2 = -13
a4 -= a3 = 8 - -13 = -5
a4 -= a3 = -5 - -13 = -8
a3 = a3 = -13
a4 += a4 = -8 + -8 = -16
a4 += a4 = -16 + -16 = -32
a4 += a2 = -32 + -5 = -37
a3 -= a2 = -13 - -5 = -8
a2 += a3 = -5 + -8 = -13
a4 -= a2 = -37 - -13 = -50
a4 += a2 = -50 + -13 = -63
a3 -= a4 = -8 - -63 = 55
a4 = a2 = -13
a3 += a2 = 55 + -13 = 42
a1 -= a4 = -18 - -13 = -31
a3 -= a4 = 42 - -13 = 55
\end{code}

a4 = -13

Answer: You have 17 lines of Python code, but only 16 in your simulation.

You have:

\begin{code}
a3 -= a3
a3 += a4
a3 = a3
\end{code}

But that is the same as:

\begin{code}
a3 += a4
\end{code}

So the two lines after the first line of your simulation are not needed.

If you do it in the correct order, you get:

\begin{code}
a2 = -5
a3 = 7
a4 = -3
a2 -= a4
a4 += a4
a3 -= a2
a3 -= a2
a2 += a3
a4 -= a2
a3 += a3
a3 += a4
a2 += a3
a4 -= a2
a3 += a2
a4 -= a3
a4 += a2
a2 += a4
a3 += a4
a2 -= a3
a3 += a3
a3 -= a4
a4 += a3

a2 = -1
a3 = 0
a4 = -4
\end{code}

Comment: Thank you! I should have noticed that

Answer: You're missing a line in your simulation. In the original code,

\begin{code}
a3 -= a3
a3 += a4
a3 = a3
\end{code}

is equivalent to

\begin{code}
a3 = a4
\end{code}

Therefore, you're missing

\begin{code}
a4 -= a2
\end{code}

which will make `a4 == -8`.

This code is simply making a bunch of reassignments of variables. It is only using the variables 'a0' through 'a4'.

For example, the first line 'a0=-10' sets the value of 'a0' to -10. The second line 'a1=-9' sets the value of 'a1' to -9. 

The third line 'a2=1' sets the value of 'a2' to 1. The fourth line 'a3=-1' sets the value of 'a3' to -1. and the fifth line 'a4=6' sets the value of 'a4' to 6.

The sixth line 'a3 += a4' sets the value of 'a3' to 6. The seventh line 'a2 = a4' sets the value of 'a2' to 6. 

The eighth line 'a4 += a3' sets the value of 'a4' to 12. The ninth line 'a4 -= a2' sets the value of 'a4' to 6.

The tenth line 'a3 -= a4' sets the value of 'a3' to 0. The eleventh line 'a4 = a2' sets the value of 'a4' to 6.

The twelfth line 'a2 = a4' sets the value of 'a2' to 6. The thirteenth line 'a4 += a3' sets the value of 'a4' to 6.

The fourteenth line 'a3 += a4' sets the value of 'a3' to 12. The fifteenth line 'a4 += a3' sets the value of 'a4' to 18. 

The sixteenth line 'a4 += a2' sets the value of 'a4' to 24. The seventeenth line 'a0 = a1' sets the value of 'a0' to -9.

The eighteenth line 'a2 -= a3' sets the value of 'a2' to -12. The nineteenth line 'a1 -= a0' sets the value of 'a1' to -18.

The twentieth line 'a1 = a0' sets the value of 'a1' to -9. The twenty-first line 'a3 += a1' sets the value of 'a3' to 0.

The twenty-second line 'a2 = a4' sets the value of 'a2' to 24. The twenty-third line 'a0 = a1' sets the value of 'a0' to -9.

The twenty-fourth line 'a3 -= a0' sets the value of 'a3' to 9. The twenty-fifth line 'a1 -= a0' sets the value of 'a1' to -18.

The twenty-sixth line 'a3 -= a2' sets the value of 'a3' to -12. The twenty-seventh line 'a1 += a0' sets the value of 'a1' to -9.

The twenty-eighth line 'a2 = a3' sets the value of 'a2' to -12. The twenty-ninth line 'a1 -= a0' sets the value of 'a1' to -18.

The thirtieth line 'a2 -= a1' sets the value of 'a2' to 9. The thirty-first line 'a3 += a2' sets the value of 'a3' to 9.

Answer: Here are the relevant lines of code:

\begin{code}
a0 = a4
a0 = a0
a1 = a1
a0 += a4
a0 += a0
a0 += a0
a0 += a2
a1 -= a3
\end{code}

After `a0 = a4` you've got `a0 = -9`, and `a1 = 1`.

After `a0 = a0` and `a1 = a1` you've got the same values as before.

After `a0 += a4` you've got `a0 = -18`, and `a1 = 1`.

After `a0 += a0` you've got `a0 = -36`, and `a1 = 1`.

After `a0 += a0` you've got `a0 = -72`, and `a1 = 1`.

After `a0 += a2` you've got `a0 = -75`, and `a1 = 1`.

After `a1 -= a3` you've got `a0 = -75`, and `a1 = 3`.

So `a4` is `-75`, and you're getting the right answer.

\strong{1.} `a1 += a3` so `a1 = -8 + -10 = -18`

\strong{2.} `a0 = a4` so `a0 = 8`

\strong{3.} `a1 -= a4` so `a1 = -18 - 8 = -26`

\strong{4.} `a0 = a1` so `a0 = -26`

\strong{5.} `a1 += a0` so `a1 = -26 + -26 = -52`

\strong{6.} `a0 += a3` so `a0 = -26 + -10 = -36`

\strong{7.} `a0 = a1` so `a0 = -52`

\strong{8.} `a1 += a2` so `a1 = -52 - 7 = -59`

\strong{9.} `a1 = a3` so `a1 = -10`

\strong{10.} `a0 -= a1` so `a0 = -52 - -10 = -42`

\strong{11.} `a0 -= a2` so `a0 = -42 - -7 = -35`

\strong{12.} `a0 -= a2` so `a0 = -35 - -7 = -28`

\strong{13.} `a1 += a4` so `a1 = -10 + 8 = 8`

\strong{14.} `a1 += a4` so `a1 = 8 + 8 = 16`

\strong{15.} `a0 = a2` so `a0 = -7`

\strong{16.} `a1 -= a3` so `a1 = 16 - -10 = 6`

\strong{17.} `a3 = a4` so `a3 = 8`

\strong{18.} `a3 -= a2` so `a3 = 8 - -7 = 15`

\strong{19.} `a3 = a3` so `a3 = 15`

\strong{20.} `a4 -= a3` so `a4 = 8 - 15 = -7`

\strong{21.} `a4 = a3` so `a4 = 15`

\strong{22.} `a3 -= a2` so `a3 = 15 - -7 = 22`

\strong{23.} `a2 = a3` so `a2 = 22`

\strong{24.} `a2 -= a4` so `a2 = 22 -2_2

Comment: This is a homework assignment, you should be doing this yourself.

Comment: Note: `a4 = a2` will not be the same as `a2 = a4`

Comment: @cricket_007: yes, but in this case, it appears to be the same.

Comment: @cricket_007: yes, I've read the code, and it appears not to matter. I've added your suggestion to my answer, though.

Comment: @MartijnPieters Ah, I see. True

Answer: Replace the `a4 -= a2` line with `a4 -= a4`

\begin{code}
a0=-1; a1=6; a2=-4; a3=-3; a4=-5
a2 += a3
a3 += a2
a2 -= a4
a3 += a2
a4 += a2
a4 = a2
a2 = a4
a4 -= a4
a4 += a4
a2 -= a4
a3 = a4
a3 += a4
a4 = a3
a3 += a1
a3 = a3
a2 += a0
a3 = a3
a0 -= a1
a3 += a3
a0 += a4
a1 -= a4
a0 += a3
a2 = a4
a0 = a2
a1 -= a2
a3 += a1
a2 = a0
\end{code}

This will result in `a4` being `2` at the end.

Comment: @vaultah: ah, yes, I missed the `a2 = a4` line. `a4` never is assigned to.

Answer: a4 = 2

<exercise>
The function below is used to calculate how much money you will have in your bank account at the end of the year if you follow the 50/30/20 rule. The rule states that 50% of your income should go towards necessities, 30% towards discretionary spending, and 20% towards saving for retirement. The function takes as input the percentage of your income that you spend on necessities and the percentage that you spend on saving for retirement. The savings percentage is assumed to be the remaining amount of your income.

def retirement_savings(savings_percentage,necessities_percentage):
    income = 10000
    savings = income * savings_percentage / 100
    discretionary = income * (100 - (savings_percentage + necessities_percentage)) / 100
    return savings + discretionary


Fill in the blanks so that the function retirement_savings returns the amount of money you will have in your bank account at the end of the year if you follow the 50/30/20 rule with 60% of your income going towards necessities and 20% towards saving for retirement.

<choice>
<opt text="retirement_savings(20,60)">

This does not work because the function is defined to take the saving percentage first and then the necessities percentage.

</opt>

<opt text="retirement_savings(60,20)" correct="true">

Great!

</opt>
</choice>
</exercise>

### 2.2.3: Truthiness

#### Question

Write a Python program to describe the truthiness of a value.

#### Solution

```python
a = 0
b = 0.0
c = []
d = {}
e = ()
f = ""
g = None
h = True
i = False
print(bool(a))
print(bool(b))
print(bool(c))
print(bool(d))
print(bool(e))
print(bool(f))
print(bool(g))
print(bool(h))
print(bool(i))
```

### 2.2.4: F-Strings

#### Question

Write a Python program to create a new string that is the reverse of the given string.

#### Solution

```python
a = "Hello, World!"
print(a[::-1])

a = "Hello, World!"
print(a.replace("Hello", "Goodbye"))

a = "Hello, World"
a += "!"
print(a)

a = "Hello, World!"
print(a.replace("World", "Python"))

a = "Hello, World!"
print(a.replace("World", "Python").replace("Hello", "Goodbye"))

a = "Hello, World!"
b = a.replace("World", "Python")
c = b.replace("Hello", "Goodbye")
print(c)
```

I'd appreciate it if you could explain what's going on here too. Thanks in advance.

Answer: Well, let's see.

`a1 -= a3` : a1 = 4 - (-5) = 9

`a1 = a2` : a1 = 6

`a1 -= a0` : a1 = 6 - 10 = -4

`a1 -= a0` : a1 = -4 - 10 = -14

`a1 = a3` : a1 = -5

`a1 += a1` : a1 = -5 + -5 = -10

`a1 = a1` : a1 = -10

`a0 += a3` : a0 = 10 + -5 = 5

`a4 = a3` : a4 = -5

`a4 += a2` : a4 = -5 + 6 = 1

`a4 += a2` : a4 = 1 + 6 = 7

`a3 -= a2` : a3 = -5 - 6 = -11

`a4 = a2` : a4 = 6

`a2 = a4` : a2 = 6

`a2 = a3` : a2 = -11

`a3 += a0` : a3 = -11 + 5 = -6

`a1 += a0` : a1 = -10 + 5 = -5

`a3 -= a2` : a3 = -6 - 6 = -12

`a3 -= a0` : a3 = -12 - 5 = -17

`a0 -= a1` : a0 = 5 - (-5) = 0

`a2 -= a1` : a2 = 6 - (-5) = 11

`a1 += a4` : a1 = -5 + 7 = 2

`a0 -= a1` : a0 = 0 - 2 = -2

`a2 -= a1` : a2 = 11 - 2 = 9

`a1 += a4` : a1 = 2 + 7 = 9

`a2 += a3` : a2 = 9 + -12 = -3

OK. I think that's right.

Comment: I think it is also right. It is a bit tedious, I just let  python do it for me and checked the code was correct.

Consider the following dictionary:

phonebook = {"John": 938477566, "Jim": 938377264, "Mary": 876786786, "Arthur": 121267579, "Sarah": 075678876}

Write a Python program that uses the keys() method to print the dictionary keys (names) and the values (phone numbers) in the order they are stored in the dictionary.
```

```
for key in phonebook.keys():
    print(key + ": " + str(phonebook[key]))
```

```
John: 938477566
Jim: 938377264
Mary: 876786786
Arthur: 121267579
Sarah: 075678876
```

```
Consider the following string:

string = "This is a sample string!"

Write a Python program that prints this string in reverse order (starting from the last character).
```

```
for i in range(len(string)-1, -1, -1):
    print(string[i], end = "")

phonebook = {"John": 938477566, "Jim": 938377264, "Mary": 876786786, "Arthur": 121267579, "Sarah": 075678876}

# Multiple Choice

1. What is the output of the following code fragment?

from math import sqrt
for x in range(1, 11):
    print(sqrt(x))

<result>1</result>

2. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(0, 5):
    print(i)

<result>0</result>

3. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(5, 0, -1):
    print(i)

<result>5</result>

4. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(1, 6):
    print(i)

<result>1</result>

5. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(0, 6, 2):
    print(i)

<result>0</result>

6. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(6, 0, -1):
    print(i)

<result>6</result>

7. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(1, 7):
    print(i)

<result>1</result>

8. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(1, 7, 2):
    print(i)

<result>1</result>

9. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(6, 0, -1):
    print(i)

<result>6</result>

10. What is the output of the following code fragment?

for i in range(0, 7):
    print(i)

<result>0</result>

# Short Answer

a = 12
b = a
a += 1

def f():
    return 42

f = 3

<result>3</result>

def f():
    return 42

f = f()
answer = f

    return 42

f = 3
f = f()

Answer: The question is asking you to simulate a Python program (i.e. what would be the values of the variables if this program was run).

So you just have to follow the code line by line and see what would happen.

For example, when you see

\begin{code}
a2 += a3
\end{code}

You know that `a2` is going to be incremented by the value of `a3` (which is -3).

Then you have

\begin{code}
a3 = a2
\end{code}

Which means `a3` will now be equal to `a2`, which was equal to `-6`.

And so on.

Answer: The instructions are pretty straightforward. You're supposed to run the code, but instead of assigning values to variables, you're supposed to write the value of each variable after the assignment is executed, and then run the assignment.

Answer: \begin{code}
import dis

def f():
    a0=-2; a1=-9; a2=-7; a3=5; a4=4
    a1 = a0
    a0 = a4
    a0 = a3
    a1 = a0
    a0 -= a4
    a0 = a4
    a0 -= a3
    a2 = a2
    a4 -= a2
    a4 -= a3
    a2 += a3
    a2 = a4
    a4 -= a2
    a4 -= a3
    a4 -= a2
    a4 += a3
    a3 -= a2
    a3 -= a2
    a2 -= a0
    a2 = a4
    a0 -= a1
    a3 -= a0
    a2 += a3
    a3 -= a1
    a3 -= a1
    a1 += a2
    a1 -= a4
    a1 = a4
    a1 = a3
    a2 += a1

dis.dis(f)
"""
  1           0 LOAD_CONST               1 (-2)
              3 STORE_FAST               0 (a0)

  2           6 LOAD_CONST               2 (-9)
              9 STORE_FAST               1 (a1)

  3          12 LOAD_CONST               3 (-7)
             15 STORE_FAST               2 (a2)

  4          18 LOAD_CONST               4 (5)
             21 STORE_FAST               3 (a3)

  5          24 LOAD_CONST               5 (4)
             27 STORE_FAST               4 (a4)

  6          30 LOAD_FAST                0 (a0)
             33 STORE_FAST               1 (a1)

Comment: I just need to know what a4 equals at the end. I'm not sure if I should be using the values of a0, a1, a2, and a3 to calculate a4. I'm not sure how to use the information given to me to solve this problem.

Comment: You're just trying to follow the instructions for each line.  Think hard about what each line is doing and what the current values of the variables are.  For example, the first line is `a0 += a3`, which means `a0 = a0 + a3`.  Since `a0` is 7 and `a3` is 1, `a0` becomes 8.  The next line is `a1 = a0`, which means that `a1` now also is 8.  And so on.  You have to keep track of what each variable is equal to and make sure you do the math correctly.

Answer: You're going to have to follow each line and do the math.  The `+=` operator is "add and assign" so `a0 += a1` means `a0 = a0 + a1`.  The order is important.  This means the next line (after `a0 += a1`) is `a1 = a0`.  So `a1` becomes the value of `a0` which is now 8 (since `a0` was 7 and `a1` was 2).  Then the next line is `a1 += a0` which means `a1` becomes `a1 + a0` which is `8 + 8` which is 16.  Then the next line is `a0 = a2` which means `a0` becomes the value of `a2` which is 9.  Then the next line is `a0 += a1` which means `a0` becomes `a0 + a1` which is 9 + 16 which is 25.  Then the next line is `a0 = a2` which means `a0` becomes 9 again.  Then the next line is `a0 += a2` which means `a0` becomes 9 + 9 which is 18.  Then the next line is `a0 = a2` which means `a0` becomes 9 again.  Then the next line is `a0 += a2` which means `a0` becomes 9 + 9 which is 18.  Then the next line is `a1 = a2` which means `a1` becomes 9.  Then the next line is `a1 += a2` which means `a1` becomes 9 + 9 which is 18.  Then the next line is `a1 += a4` which means `a1` becomes 18 + (-3) which is 15.  Then the next line is `a4 = a4` which is a no-op.  Then the next line is `a2 += a4` which means `a2` becomes 9 + (-3) which is 6.  Then the next line is `a3 = a2` which means `a3` becomes 6.  Then the next line is `a3 = a3` which is a no-op.  Then the next line is `a4 = a3` which means `a4` becomes 6.  Then the next line is `a4 += a2` which means `a4` becomes 6 + 6 which is 12.  Then the next line is `a4 = a2` which means `a4` becomes 6 again.  Then the next line is `a4 -= a2` which means `a4` becomes 6 - 6 which is 0.  Then the next line is `a4 -= a2` which means `a4` becomes 0 - 6 which is -6.  Then the next line is `a2 = a3` which means `a2` becomes 6.  Then the next line is `a3 -= a4` which means `a3` becomes 6 - -6 which is 12.  Then the next line is `a4 -= a3` which means `a4` becomes -6 - 12 which is -18.  Then the next line is `a4 -= a3` which means `a4` becomes -18 - 12 which is -30.  Then the next line is `a2 = a3` which means `a2` becomes 12.  Then the next line is `a4 += a4` which means `a4` becomes -30 + -30 which is -60.  Then the next line is `a0 += a4` which means `a0` becomes 18 + -60 which is -42.  Then the next line is `a2 -= a4` which means `a2` becomes 12 - -60 which is 72.

So at the end `a4` is equal to -60.

I turned these into variables so I could keep track of them easier.

variables = {
    "a0":3,
    "a1":0,
    "a2":-4,
    "a3":7,
    "a4":2
}

for line in lines:
    line = line.strip()
    if "=" in line:
        left, right = line.split("=")
        variables[left] = int(right)
    else:
        left, right = line.split("-=")
        variables[left] -= int(right)

for line in lines:
    line = line.strip()
    if "=" in line:
        left, right = line.split("=")
        variables[left] = int(right)
    else:
        left, right = line.split("+=")
        variables[left] += int(right)

print(variables["a4"])
